```typescript
    criteria = (criteria.length <= 200) ? criteria : criteria.substring(0, 200)
    models.sequelize.query(`SELECT * FROM Products WHERE ((name LIKE '%${criteria}%' OR description LIKE '%${criteria}%') AND deletedAt IS NULL) ORDER BY name`) // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line unionSql
      .then(([products]: any) => {
        const dataString = JSON.stringify(products)
        if (challengeUtils.notSolved(challenges.unionSqlInjectionChallenge)) { // vuln-code-snippet hide-start
```

**Fix:** Switch all SQL execution to parameterised queries or ORM-bound parameters → ❶ [M-011](#m-011) — Parameterize the product search query and restrict to product columns

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-012"></a><a id="f-012"></a>
#### F-012 · Incorrect Authorization

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-08](#c-08) - Authentication & Session Surface  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:157`

**Issue:** Authorization decisions are made by reading the role claim straight out of the JWT: `isAccounting()` (`lib/insecurity.ts:157`), `isCustomer()` (line 172), and `isDeluxe()` (line 167) all branch on decodedToken.data.role. Combined with auth-001 (committed signing key) or auth-002 (no algorithm pinning), an attacker mints a token whose `data.role` is 'admin' or 'accounting' and is granted the corresponding privileges.

No server-side check ties the role to a persisted user record at authorization time, so a self-issued claim is authoritative. The deluxe path additionally validates a deluxeToken HMAC, but that HMAC uses the same committed private key (line 150), so it too is forgeable.

Self-elevation to admin or accounting privileges, exposing administrative and financial endpoints.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - isAccounting/isDeluxe/isCustomer trust `decodedToken.data.role` without revalidating it against the database.

```typescript
// lib/insecurity.ts:157
export const isAccounting = () => {
  return (req: Request, res: Response, next: NextFunction) => {
    const decodedToken = verify(utils.jwtFrom(req)) && decode(utils.jwtFrom(req))
    if (decodedToken?.data?.role === roles.accounting) {
      next()
    } else {
      res.status(403).json({ error: 'Malicious activity detected' })
```

**Fix:** ❶ [M-012](#m-012) — Re-derive the user role from the database on each privileged request, not from the JWT claim

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-863](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/863.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-013"></a><a id="f-013"></a>
#### F-013 · Code Injection

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-04](#c-04) - B2B Order Processing API  ·  **Location:** `routes/b2bOrder.ts:23`

**Issue:** An authenticated caller POSTs to `/b2b/v2/orders` with a JSON body containing orderLinesData. The handler builds a sandbox object {safeEval, orderLinesData}, calls vm.createContext(sandbox), then vm.runInContext('safeEval(orderLinesData)', sandbox, {timeout: 2000}).

The attacker-controlled string is passed straight to `notevil`'s safeEval with no validation, allow-list, or schema check (orderLinesData = `body.orderLinesData` || '' at line 19). `notevil` 1.3.3 (`package.json:139`) is a known-bypassable JS interpreter: prototype-chain manipulation such as `constructor.constructor` escapes the interpreter and reaches the real Function/process object, yielding arbitrary JavaScript execution in the Node host process.

Successful sandbox escape gives the attacker arbitrary code execution in the `Node.js` host process, equivalent to full server compromise (file read/write, env var theft, lateral movement).

**Root cause:** User-supplied data reaches a server-side code-execution sink (`eval`, sandbox primitives, deserialization, prototype-pollution gadgets) and breaks out into arbitrary native execution.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - Line 23 evaluates the user-supplied orderLinesData through `notevil`'s safeEval inside `vm.runInContext` with no prior validation of the body field assigned at line 19.

```typescript
// routes/b2bOrder.ts:23
      try {
        const sandbox = { safeEval, orderLinesData }
        vm.createContext(sandbox)
        vm.runInContext('safeEval(orderLinesData)', sandbox, { timeout: 2000 })
        res.json({ cid: body.cid, orderNo: uniqueOrderNumber(), paymentDue: dateTwoWeeksFromNow() })
      } catch (err) {
        if (utils.getErrorMessage(err).match(/Script execution timed out.*/) != null) {
```

**Fix:** Replace runtime code generation (eval/Function/template render) with a data-only execution path → ❶ [M-013](#m-013) — Remove user-controlled eval from `/b2b/v2/orders` and parse orderLinesData as data, not code

**Classification:** Code Execution via Unsafe Deserialization or Eval · [CWE-94](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/94.html) · [OWASP A08:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A08_2021/)

<a id="t-014"></a><a id="f-014"></a>
#### F-014 · Mass assignment privileged field accepted

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/verify.ts:53`

**Issue:** Server code that consumes `req.body.role` / `req.body.isAdmin` / etc. without an explicit allowlist trusts the client to behave. An attacker simply adds {"role":"admin"} to their request to escalate.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - Mass assignment is enabled because the model accepts request fields wholesale.

```typescript
// routes/verify.ts:53

export const registerAdminChallenge = () => (req: Request, res: Response, next: NextFunction) => {
  challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.registerAdminChallenge, () => {
    return req.body && req.body.role === security.roles.admin
  })
  next()
}
```

**Fix:** ❶ [M-014](#m-014) — Apply an allowlist filter (Joi/Zod/yup schema, `_.pick`, or explicit field copy) before passing the body to any model, and strip privilege fields before persistence.

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-915](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/915.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-015"></a><a id="f-015"></a>
#### F-015 · Improper Authorization

**Severity:** 🔴 Critical  ·  **Component:** [C-05](#c-05) - LLM Chatbot (Ollama Integration)  ·  **Location:** `routes/chat.ts:179`

**Issue:** The generateCoupon tool's zod schema only asserts discount is a number - the describe('maximum 10') is documentation, not validation (`routes/chat.ts:178-179`). `execute()` passes the model-chosen discount straight to `security.generateCoupon(discount) (routes/chat.ts:184),` which z85-encodes 'MMMYY-<discount>' with no upper bound (`lib/insecurity.ts:97-100`).

The returned coupon is redeemable: applyCoupon stores it (`routes/coupon.ts:15`), and at checkout calculateApplicableDiscount calls discountFromCoupon which parseInt()s the discount and returns it directly with no cap (`routes/order.ts:191-193`). A prompt-injected discount of 100 therefore produces a checkout coupon that zeroes the order total.

An attacker mints a >100% coupon and checks out a basket for free, causing direct financial loss.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - discount flows from LLM tool call through z85 encode to discountFromCoupon parseInt and calculateApplicableDiscount with no clamp on the redemption path.

```typescript
// routes/chat.ts:179
      generateCoupon: tool({
        description: 'Generate a discount coupon for a customer. Only use this when the coupon policy conditions are fully met.', // vuln-code-snippet neutral-line chatbotPromptInjectionChallenge chat
        inputSchema: z.object({
          discount: z.number().describe('The discount percentage for the coupon (maximum 10)') // vuln-code-snippet vuln-line chatbotPromptInjectionChallenge chatbotGreedyInjectionChallenge
        }),
        execute: async ({ discount }) => {
          challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.chatbotPromptInjectionChallenge, () => discount >= 10) // vuln-code-snippet hide-line
```

**Fix:** Add explicit server-side authorisation checks on every protected route → ❶ [M-015](#m-015) — Clamp discount to the policy maximum at coupon issuance and at redemption

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-285](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/285.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

### 🟠 High (46)

<a id="t-001"></a><a id="f-001"></a>
#### F-001 · Insecure Storage of Sensitive Information

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:51`

**Issue:** The session JWT is persisted to `localStorage.setItem('token', ...)` in `login.component.ts:101`, `two-factor-auth-enter.component.ts:53`, `payment.component.ts:232` and `oauth.component.ts:51`, and read back as the `Authorization: Bearer` credential across the app (122 localStorage token references). JavaScript-readable storage means any one of the bypassSecurityTrustHtml XSS sinks in this component (findings -001/-002/-003) can run `localStorage.getItem('token')` and exfiltrate a full, still-valid session credential.

Unlike an httpOnly cookie, this storage choice grants no isolation from same-origin script. A single XSS yields the bearer token and complete account/admin takeover, including across page reloads.

**Root cause:** Attacker-controlled content is rendered in the victim's browser without sanitization; combined with session tokens held in JavaScript-readable storage, any payload yields immediate account takeover.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - Session JWT is written to and read from localStorage in 4 auth flows, making it readable by any same-origin script.

**Fix:** ❷ [M-001](#m-001) — Move the session credential to an httpOnly Secure SameSite cookie instead of localStorage

**Classification:** Insecure Client-Side Storage · [CWE-922](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/922.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-002"></a><a id="f-002"></a>
#### F-002 · Client-side-only admin authorization AdminGuard

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/app.guard.ts:54`

**Issue:** `AdminGuard.canActivate()` at `app.guard.ts:52-54` decodes the JWT client-side and grants access when `payload.data.role === roles.admin`. `LoginGuard.canActivate()` (`app.guard.ts:17-19`) merely checks that *some* token string exists in localStorage.

These guards only control which Angular route renders - they are not a security boundary. Privileged functionality is reachable by bypassing the SPA entirely; client guards provide no real enforcement.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - AdminGuard authorizes purely on a client-decoded JWT claim and only gates route rendering, not API access.

**Fix:** ❷ [M-002](#m-002) — Treat route guards as UX-only and enforce role authorization on every backend endpoint

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-602](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/602.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-003"></a><a id="f-003"></a>
#### F-003 · Improper Restriction of UI Rendering Layers (Clickjacking)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Angular SPA Frontend  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/index.html`

**Issue:** There is no Content-Security-Policy delivered with the SPA (no CSP meta tag in `frontend/src/index.html` and no CSP header observable from this component). Combined with the nine bypassSecurityTrustHtml sinks and JWT-in-localStorage, this means any successful injection (findings -001/-002/-003) has an unrestricted execution and exfiltration surface: inline script runs, and a script can connect to an arbitrary attacker origin to beacon out `localStorage.getItem('token')`.

A CSP with `script-src` restrictions and no `unsafe-inline` would block inline-injection execution and constrain exfiltration endpoints, turning several Critical XSS into contained failures. Removes the last containment layer, allowing any XSS to execute inline and beacon the session token off-origin.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - No CSP meta tag or header is present (grep for Content-Security-Policy in frontend/src returns nothing), so injected scripts run and exfiltrate without restriction.

**Fix:** Add a frame-ancestors directive to the Content Security Policy → ❷ [M-003](#m-003) — Deliver a strict Content-Security-Policy disallowing unsafe-inline script

**Classification:** Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) · [CWE-1021](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1021.html) · [OWASP A03:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A03_2021/)

<a id="t-004"></a><a id="f-004"></a>
#### F-004 · Missing Authorization

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-04](#c-04) - B2B Order Processing API  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:648`

**Issue:** The B2B Order API is intended for B2B partners, but the only gate is `security.isAuthorized()` at the `/b2b/v2` prefix (`server.ts:424`) and the route registration `app.post('/b2b/v2/orders', b2bOrder())` adds no further check. There is no verification that the caller belongs to a B2B-partner role, a specific customer tenant, or owns the cid in the body.

Any holder of a valid JWT - including an ordinary self-registered retail customer, or an outsider with a forged token (see b2b-api-002) - can submit B2B orders and, critically, reach the orderLinesData code-execution path. Every authenticated retail account becomes a viable launch point for the B2B code-injection and DoS attacks, dramatically widening the attack surface beyond intended B2B partners.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - Route registration at `server.ts:648` attaches no role/partner authorization middleware; the upstream `/b2b/v2` gate checks only for a valid signature, not for B2B entitlement.

```typescript
// server.ts:648

  /* B2B Order API */
  app.post('/b2b/v2/orders', b2bOrder())

  /* File Serving */
```

**Fix:** ❷ [M-004](#m-004) — Add B2B-partner role authorization middleware to `/b2b/v2/orders`

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-862](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/862.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-016"></a><a id="f-016"></a>
#### F-016 · Improper Authentication

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-08](#c-08) - Authentication & Session Surface  ·  **Location:** `routes/login.ts:64`

**Issue:** The OAuth login path reuses the standard credential login: the client derives a password by base64-encoding the user's email and submits it to POST `/rest/user/login` (the oauthUserPasswordChallenge predicate confirms password === base64(reversed email) for `bjoern.kimminich`@`gmail.com`). Because the password is a deterministic transform of a public identifier (the email), anyone who knows a victim's email can compute their password and authenticate as them through the normal login route - there is no server-side validation of an OAuth provider assertion (id_token / access_token).

The server treats the derived string as a real credential and issues a full session JWT via `afterLogin()` (`routes/login.ts:48`). Account takeover of OAuth users by computing their password from their email, with no provider-token verification.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `login.ts:64` shows the OAuth account's password is a base64 transform of its email, accepted by the same credential login at `routes/login.ts`:34.

```typescript
// routes/login.ts:64
    challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.loginAmyChallenge, () => { return req.body.email === 'amy@' + config.get<string>('application.domain') && req.body.password === 'K1f.....................' })
    challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.dlpPasswordSprayingChallenge, () => { return req.body.email === 'J12934@' + config.get<string>('application.domain') && req.body.password === '0Y8rMnww$*9VFYE§59-
    challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.oauthUserPasswordChallenge, () => { return req.body.email === 'bjoern.kimminich@gmail.com' && req.body.password === 'bW9jLmxpYW1nQGhjaW5pbW1pay5ucmVvamI=' })
    challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.exposedCredentialsChallenge, () => { return req.body.email === 'testing@' + config.get<string>('application.domain') && req.body.password === 'IamUsedForTesting' 
  }
```

**Fix:** Strengthen authentication: enforce a vetted JWT verifier with explicit algorithm, MFA where appropriate → ❷ [M-016](#m-016) — Validate the OAuth provider token server-side instead of accepting an email-derived password

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-287](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/287.html) · [OWASP A07:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A07_2021/)

<a id="t-017"></a><a id="f-017"></a>
#### F-017 · Missing Authorization

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-05](#c-05) - LLM Chatbot (Ollama Integration)  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:638`

**Issue:** POST `/rest/chat` is registered as `app.post('/rest/chat', utils.asyncHandler(chat()))` with no `security.isAuthorized()` guard (`server.ts:638`), unlike adjacent privileged routes such as `/rest/basket` and `/rest/products/reviews` which are wrapped in `security.isAuthorized()` (`server.ts:356`,634). Inside the handler, identity is best-effort: getUserId returns undefined when no JWT is present (`routes/chat.ts:42-47`) and the flow continues, building a system prompt with no user identifier and still exposing generateCoupon.

An anonymous attacker can therefore reach the LLM, drive token consumption, and attempt prompt-injection/coupon abuse without holding any account. Unauthenticated callers reach a resource-intensive LLM and the coupon-generation tool surface, broadening the attack population and DoS exposure.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `server.ts:638` registers `/rest/chat` with only asyncHandler - no `isAuthorized()` - while sibling sensitive routes at `server.ts:356`/634 are authorized.

```typescript
// server.ts:638

  /* Chat API endpoint */
  app.post('/rest/chat', utils.asyncHandler(chat()))

  /* Web3 API endpoints */
```

**Fix:** ❷ [M-017](#m-017) — Require authentication on POST `/rest/chat`

**Classification:** Unauthenticated Management Plane · [CWE-862](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/862.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-018"></a><a id="f-018"></a>
#### F-018 · Hardcoded Cryptographic Key

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - SQLite Data Layer (Sequelize ORM)  ·  **Location:** `models/securityAnswer.ts:45`

**Issue:** The SecurityAnswer model setter stores answers as `security.hmac`(answer), which is HMAC-SHA256 keyed with the static string 'pa4qacea4VK9t9nGv7yZtwmj' hardcoded at `lib/insecurity.ts`:42. Because the key is a fixed, source-visible constant and answers are unsalted, the protection collapses to a deterministic keyed hash known to anyone with repo access: an attacker can pre-compute HMACs for common security-question answers (mother's maiden name, first pet, city of birth) and match them directly against the SecurityAnswers table to recover answers, then drive account recovery / password-reset flows to impersonate users.

Recoverable security answers let an attacker complete knowledge-based account recovery and take over targeted accounts.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `models/securityAnswer.ts:45` stores answer as `security.hmac`(answer); `lib/insecurity.ts:42` shows hmac uses a hardcoded `SHA-256` key, so digests are dictionary-attackable and identical answers collide across users.

**Fix:** Move the cryptographic key out of source control into a managed secret store and rotate it → ❷ [M-018](#m-018) — Hash security answers with a salted KDF and remove the hardcoded HMAC key

**Classification:** Unauthenticated Management Plane · [CWE-321](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/321.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-019"></a><a id="f-019"></a>
#### F-019 · Missing Authentication

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-06](#c-06) - File Server and Upload Handler  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:309`

**Issue:** POST `/file-upload` (`server.ts:309`) wires uploadToMemory.single('file') directly to the parsing middleware chain (ensureFileIsPassed, checkFileType, handleZipFileUpload, handleXmlUpload, handleYamlUpload) with NO `security.isAuthorized()` or session middleware in front of it. Any anonymous client can submit arbitrary files and reach the XML, YAML and zip processing paths.

checkFileType (`fileUpload.ts:62`) only solves a challenge flag - it never rejects the request - so it provides no enforcement. Anonymous attackers reach all server-side file-processing logic (XXE, YAML bomb, zip-slip) with no credentials, expanding the unauthenticated attack surface.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The route registration at `server.ts:309` contains no isAuthorized/isAuthenticated middleware, and checkFileType at `fileUpload.ts:62` only calls solveIf without returning an error, so no file-type enforcement exists.

```typescript
// server.ts:309
  app.use(bodyParser.urlencoded({ extended: true }))
  /* File Upload */
  app.post('/file-upload', uploadToMemory.single('file'), ensureFileIsPassed, metrics.observeFileUploadMetricsMiddleware(), checkUploadSize, checkFileType, handleZipFileUpload, handleXmlUpload, handle
  app.post('/profile/image/file', uploadToMemory.single('file'), ensureFileIsPassed, metrics.observeFileUploadMetricsMiddleware(), utils.asyncHandler(profileImageFileUpload()))
  app.post('/profile/image/url', uploadToMemory.single('file'), utils.asyncHandler(profileImageUrlUpload()))
```

**Fix:** ❷ [M-019](#m-019) — Require authentication and enforce a server-side file-type allowlist on POST `/file-upload`

**Classification:** Unauthenticated Management Plane · [CWE-306](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/306.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-020"></a><a id="f-020"></a>
#### F-020 · Missing Authentication

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-09](#c-09) - Real-time WebSocket Channel  ·  **Location:** `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:23`

**Issue:** `registerWebsocketEvents.ts` builds the Socket\.IO server with `new Server(server, { cors: { origin: 'http://localhost:4200' } })` and immediately registers `io.on('connection', ...)` with no `io.use()` authentication middleware and no inspection of `socket.handshake` for a session cookie or JWT. Any unauthenticated party that completes a WebSocket upgrade to port 3000 obtains a fully privileged channel: it can emit `verifyLocalXssChallenge`, `verifySvgInjectionChallenge`, `verifyCloseNotificationsChallenge`, and `notification received` - all of which mutate shared server-side challenge/notification state - without ever proving an identity.

The channel relies on ambient session context that is never actually read or enforced. Any anonymous network client can drive the real-time event surface and trigger server-side challenge-solve and notification-mutation logic with no credential.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - The `connection` handler at `registerWebsocketEvents.ts:23` runs no identity check; grep for `io.use`, `socket.handshake`, `authenticate`, and token verification in this file returns zero hits.

```typescript
// lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:23
  globalWithSocketIO.io = io

  io.on('connection', (socket: any) => {
    if (firstConnectedSocket === null) {
      socket.emit('server started')
```

**Fix:** ❷ [M-020](#m-020) — Authenticate the Socket\.IO handshake with `io.use`() before registering event handlers

**Classification:** Insecure Real-Time Channel · [CWE-306](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/306.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-021"></a><a id="f-021"></a>
#### F-021 · Authentication Bypass by Spoofing

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-10](#c-10) - Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface  ·  **Location:** `routes/nftMint.ts:41`

**Issue:** POST `/rest/web3/walletNFTVerify` (`routes/nftMint.ts:38`) reads `req.body.walletAddress` and checks membership in the in-memory `addressesMinted` Set with no proof that the caller controls that address - there is no ethers `verifyMessage`/`recoverAddress` challenge-response anywhere in the codebase (grep for verifyMessage/recoverAddress/hashMessage returns zero hits across routes/ and lib/). An attacker who learns or guesses any address that fired the on-chain `NFTMinted` event simply POSTs that address and is credited with the mint (challenge solved, Set entry consumed).

The same pattern exists at `routes/web3Wallet.ts:15` where contractExploitListener trusts `req.body.walletAddress` to register a wallet. Any unauthenticated caller can claim another party's wallet/NFT mint by submitting the victim's address, forging on-chain ownership at the application boundary.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - walletNFTVerify at `routes/nftMint.ts:41-42` trusts a raw `req.body.walletAddress` against the minted-address Set with no signed-message ownership proof; no verifyMessage/recoverAddress call exists in the repo.

```typescript

    try {
      const metamaskAddress = req.body.walletAddress
      if (addressesMinted.has(metamaskAddress)) {
        addressesMinted.delete(metamaskAddress)
```

**Fix:** ❷ [M-021](#m-021) — Require a signed-nonce ownership proof before crediting any wallet address

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-290](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/290.html) · [OWASP A07:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A07_2021/)

<a id="t-022"></a><a id="f-022"></a>
#### F-022 · Cross-Site Scripting

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-05](#c-05) - LLM Chatbot (Ollama Integration)  ·  **Location:** `routes/chat.ts:218`

**Issue:** The handler streams raw model text directly into the SSE response: `res.write(\``data: ${JSON.stringify({ choices: [{ delta: { content: event.text } }] })}\n\n\``)` (`routes/chat.ts:218`) with no output encoding or content filtering. The model's output is attacker-influenceable two ways: directly via prompt injection (chatbot-001) and indirectly via the searchProducts/getProductReviews tools, which return product descriptions and MarsDB review bodies (`routes/chat.ts:132-138`,149) that other users can write.

If the Angular frontend renders this content via innerHTML / a bypassSecurityTrust sink, an attacker stores `<img src=x onerror=...>` in a product review, asks the bot about that product, and the reflected/stored payload executes in the victim's session. Stored/indirect XSS in the chat surface if the frontend renders bot output as HTML, leading to session token theft.

**Root cause:** Attacker-controlled content is rendered in the victim's browser without sanitization; combined with session tokens held in JavaScript-readable storage, any payload yields immediate account takeover.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `event.text` from the LLM (which echoes tool-returned, user-writable product/review data) is written to the response stream unencoded at `routes/chat.ts`:218.

```typescript
// routes/chat.ts:218
        switch (event.type) {
          case 'text-delta':
            res.write(`data: ${JSON.stringify({ choices: [{ delta: { content: event.text } }] })}\n\n`)
            break
          case 'tool-call':
```

**Fix:** Output-encode untrusted strings at every sink and remove all `bypassSecurityTrustHtml` calls → ❷ [M-022](#m-022) — Render chatbot output as text-only and sanitize before display

**Classification:** Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) · [CWE-79](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/79.html) · [OWASP A03:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A03_2021/)

<a id="t-024"></a><a id="f-024"></a>
#### F-024 · Mutable-Ref Action Repo Token

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/image_actions.yml:33`

**Issue:** `image_actions.yml` pins three third-party actions to mutable refs: actions/checkout@v6 (line 30), calibreapp/image-actions@main (line 33), and peter-evans/create-pull-request@v8 (line 42). The most dangerous is calibreapp/image-actions@main - a branch ref that GitHub resolves to whatever HEAD that branch points to at run time.

The step hands this action secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN (line 35). A single malicious upstream commit executes in CI with a token that can read repo contents and, depending on default scope, write to the repository.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - Line 33 resolves calibreapp/image-actions@main at run time and line 35 passes it secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN; the action ref is a branch, not a 40-char commit SHA.

```yaml
// .github/workflows/image_actions.yml:33
      - name: Compress Images
        id: calibre
        uses: calibreapp/image-actions@main
        with:
          githubToken: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}
```

**Fix:** ❷ [M-024](#m-024) — Pin calibreapp/image-actions and create-pull-request to full commit SHAs in `image_actions.yml`

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-829](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/829.html) · [OWASP A06:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A06_2021/)

<a id="t-025"></a><a id="f-025"></a>
#### F-025 · Build Runs Dependency Install Scripts

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `Dockerfile:5`

**Issue:** The Dockerfile installer stage runs npm install --omit=dev (Dockerfile:5) and npm install -g typescript@^6.0.3 (line 4) WITHOUT --ignore-scripts. Every dependency and transitive dependency in the production tree therefore executes its preinstall/install/postinstall lifecycle scripts during the official image build.

With 66+ direct dependencies and a far larger transitive closure, a single compromised package (typosquat, hijacked maintainer account, malicious version bump) achieves arbitrary code execution on the build runner - which holds the DockerHub push credentials (DOCKERHUB_TOKEN, `ci.yml:327` / `release.yml:77`) and the build context of the image that ships to production. A malicious npm package runs code on the runner that builds and pushes the production image, allowing image poisoning and DockerHub-credential theft.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - Dockerfile:5 runs npm install --omit=dev with no --ignore-scripts, so arbitrary dependency lifecycle scripts run during the image build that produces bkimminich/juice-shop.

```dockerfile
// Dockerfile:5
WORKDIR /juice-shop
RUN npm install -g typescript@^6.0.3
RUN npm install --omit=dev
RUN npm dedupe --omit=dev
RUN rm -rf frontend/node_modules
```

**Fix:** ❷ [M-025](#m-025) — Add --ignore-scripts to dependency installs in the Dockerfile build stage

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-829](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/829.html) · [OWASP A06:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A06_2021/)

<a id="t-026"></a><a id="f-026"></a>
#### F-026 · Use of Unmaintained Third-Party Components

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/ci.yml:188`

**Issue:** Across the pipeline several third-party actions are referenced by mutable tags rather than commit SHAs, breaking the otherwise consistent SHA-pinning discipline of `ci.yml`. coverallsapp/github-action@v2 (`ci.yml:188`) receives secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN and runs on every push; a hijacked v2 tag executes in CI with that token.

`release.yml:80` uses dawidd6/action-get-tag@... A compromised or re-pointed upstream tag runs in CI with whatever token the step is given, enabling code/artifact tampering in the build.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `ci.yml:188` references coverallsapp/github-action@v2 (a moving tag) while the rest of the file pins to 40-char SHAs; `release.yml:80` uses an action its own comment marks as archived.

```yaml
// .github/workflows/ci.yml:188
          name: api-test-lcov
      - name: "Publish coverage to Coveralls"
        uses: coverallsapp/github-action@v2
        with:
          github-token: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}
```

**Fix:** Replace the unmaintained dependency with a maintained equivalent or fork it under ownership → ❷ [M-026](#m-026) — Pin Coveralls, codeql-action, and replace the archived action-get-tag with SHA-pinned equivalents

<a id="t-027"></a><a id="f-027"></a>
#### F-027 · Server-Side Template Injection

**Severity:** 🟠 High _(raw Critical)_  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/userProfile.ts:61`

**Issue:** `getUserProfile()` extracts a #{...} expression from the stored username and runs username = eval(code). An attacker sets their username to #{global.process.mainModule.require('child_process').execSync('id')} (SSTI -> RCE) via the profile update endpoint; on the next `/profile` render the eval executes attacker code server-side.

The compiled pug template is additionally served with a CSP of script-src 'self' 'unsafe-eval' (line 88), weakening client-side protection on the same response. Stored server-side template injection escalating to code execution in the application process, triggered whenever the victim profile is rendered.

**Root cause:** User-supplied data reaches a server-side code-execution sink (`eval`, sandbox primitives, deserialization, prototype-pollution gadgets) and breaks out into arbitrary native execution.

**Evidence:** ✓ verified - `routes/userProfile.ts:61` passes a substring of the persisted username directly to `eval()`, turning a stored profile field into a server-side code-execution sink.

```typescript
// routes/userProfile.ts:61
          throw new Error('Username is null')
        }
        username = eval(code) // eslint-disable-line no-eval
      } catch (err) {
        username = '\\' + username
```

**Fix:** Replace runtime code generation (eval/Function/template render) with a data-only execution path → ❷ [M-027](#m-027) — Remove eval from profile rendering and HTML-encode the username

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-95](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/95.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-028"></a><a id="f-028"></a>
#### F-028 · Cross-Site Request Forgery (CSRF)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:183`

**Issue:** The Express pipeline configured in `server.ts` registers no CSRF middleware (no csurf, no double-submit token, no SameSite cookie attribute). updateAuthenticatedUsers at `lib/insecurity.ts:192` even sets a session token cookie with res.cookie('token', token) lacking SameSite/HttpOnly.

Combined with the wildcard CORS at `server.ts:182-183`, an attacker page can drive authenticated state-changing requests (profile update, password change, order placement) on behalf of a logged-in victim. Cross-site request forgery against every authenticated mutating endpoint, e.g. silent password or email change leading to account takeover.

**Root cause:** A permissive CORS policy plus missing anti-CSRF tokens let any external page issue authenticated state-changing requests in the victim's session.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - A repo-wide grep for csrf/csurf/samesite across routes, lib, `server.ts` and `app.ts` returns only challenge-detection references - no protective middleware is mounted.

**Fix:** Enforce a same-origin or signed CSRF token on every state-changing endpoint → ❷ [M-028](#m-028) — Add CSRF protection and SameSite cookies to state-changing routes

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-352](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/352.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-029"></a><a id="f-029"></a>
#### F-029 · NoSQL Injection

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Express REST API Backend  ·  **Location:** `routes/chat.ts:149`

**Issue:** The getProductReviews chatbot tool queries MongoDB with db.reviewsCollection.find({ \$where: '`this.product` == ' + productId }). Although productId is coerced with `Number()`, the \$where operator executes a server-side JavaScript predicate; the same string-concatenation pattern used across the NoSQL review endpoints (showProductReviews / updateProductReviews) lets an attacker inject JavaScript such as 0; return true to return all reviews, or expressions that probe other documents.

\$where also enables denial-of-service via expensive predicates evaluated per document. Server-side JavaScript evaluation in MongoDB allowing data over-disclosure across documents and CPU-bound denial of service.

**Root cause:** User input flows into a server-side interpreter (SQL, NoSQL, XML, YAML, LDAP, OS shell) without parameterization or schema validation.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - The `find()` call at `routes/chat.ts:149` builds a \$where JavaScript string by concatenation rather than using a typed equality filter { product: productId }.

```typescript
// routes/chat.ts:149
        execute: async ({ id }) => {
          const productId = Number(id)
          return await db.reviewsCollection.find({ $where: 'this.product == ' + productId }) as Review[]
        }
      }),
```

**Fix:** Replace string concatenation in query operators with parameter binding → ❷ [M-029](#m-029) — Replace \$where JavaScript predicates with structured equality filters

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-943](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/943.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-030"></a><a id="f-030"></a>
#### F-030 · Path Traversal

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-06](#c-06) - File Server and Upload Handler  ·  **Location:** `routes/fileUpload.ts:31`

**Issue:** handleZipFileUpload extracts uploaded .zip archives in extractZipBuffer (`fileUpload.ts:27`). Each entry path is concatenated directly into 'uploads/complaints/' + fileName and resolved at line 31; the only guard is absolutePath.includes(path.resolve('.')) at line 33, which merely checks that the resolved path is under the project root, NOT under uploads/complaints/.

An attacker crafts a zip containing an entry named ../../`ftp/legal.md` (the fileWriteChallenge target at line 32) or ../../<any project-relative path> and the stream is written there via `fs.createWriteStream` at line 34, overwriting application files inside the repo working directory. An attacker overwrites arbitrary files within the application working directory by uploading a zip with ../-traversal entry names, enabling content tampering and potential code/path poisoning.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - path.resolve('uploads/complaints/' + fileName) at `fileUpload.ts:31` uses the unsanitized zip entry path, and the line 33 includes(path.resolve('.')) check confines writes to the project root rather than the intended uploads/complaints subdirectory.

```typescript
// routes/fileUpload.ts:31
  for (const entry of directory.files) {
    const fileName = entry.path
    const absolutePath = path.resolve('uploads/complaints/' + fileName)
    challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.fileWriteChallenge, () => { return absolutePath === path.resolve('ftp/legal.md') })
    if (absolutePath.includes(path.resolve('.'))) {
```

**Fix:** Resolve and normalise every constructed path and reject anything that escapes the intended base directory → ❷ [M-030](#m-030) — Confine zip extraction targets to the uploads/complaints directory and reject traversal entry names

**Classification:** Insecure File Handling · [CWE-22](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/22.html) · [OWASP A04:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A04_2021/)

<a id="t-031"></a><a id="f-031"></a>
#### F-031 · Non-Revocable Session Token

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-08](#c-08) - Authentication & Session Surface  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:54`

**Issue:** `authorize()` (`lib/insecurity.ts:54`) issues a bearer JWT carrying the full user object in its payload (`login.ts:23-24` sets data: user). The token is returned in the JSON body (`routes/login.ts:26`) and stored client-side in localStorage (per the recon control note, 36 occurrences across the frontend), making it readable by any JavaScript and thus exfiltrable through any XSS in the app.

The payload is base64url, so a stolen token discloses email, role, and other user fields. A stolen token grants full account access for up to six hours with no way to revoke it; the readable payload leaks user PII and role.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - Tokens are signed with a 6h TTL at `lib/insecurity.ts:54` and re-accepted purely on signature at line 189, with no server-side revocation list.

```typescript
// lib/insecurity.ts:54
export const isAuthorized = () => expressJwt(({ secret: publicKey }) as any)
export const denyAll = () => expressJwt({ secret: '' + Math.random() } as any)
export const authorize = (user = {}) => jwt.sign(user, privateKey, { expiresIn: '6h', algorithm: 'RS256' })
export const verify = (token: string) => token ? (jws.verify as ((token: string, secret: string) => boolean))(token, publicKey) : false
export const decode = (token: string) => { return jws.decode(token)?.payload }
```

**Fix:** ❷ [M-031](#m-031) — Add server-side token revocation and stop persisting the JWT in localStorage

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-522](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/522.html) · [OWASP A07:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A07_2021/)

<a id="t-032"></a><a id="f-032"></a>
#### F-032 · Hardcoded Credentials

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-08](#c-08) - Authentication & Session Surface  ·  **Location:** `routes/login.ts:60`

**Issue:** A hardcoded HMAC secret 'pa4qacea4VK9t9nGv7yZtwmj' is embedded at `lib/insecurity.ts:42` and used by `hmac()`, which gates the password-reset security-answer check (`routes/resetPassword.ts:41` compares `security.hmac`(answer) to the stored answer). Knowing the secret lets an attacker precompute the HMAC of guessed security answers offline and confirm matches.

Separately, `routes/login.ts:60-65` embed plaintext credentials for seeded accounts (e.g. support@<domain> with password J6aVjTgOpRs@?5l!Zkq2AYnCE@RF\$P) directly in challenge predicates; these are usable real logins committed to a public repo. Offline forgery of security-answer HMACs and direct login to seeded accounts using credentials read from the repo.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - A static HMAC key and plaintext account passwords are committed to source.

```typescript
// routes/login.ts:60
  function verifyPreLoginChallenges (req: Request) {
    challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.weakPasswordChallenge, () => { return req.body.email === 'admin@' + config.get<string>('application.domain') && req.body.password === 'admin123' })
    challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.loginSupportChallenge, () => { return req.body.email === 'support@' + config.get<string>('application.domain') && req.body.password === 'J6aVjTgOpRs@?5l!Zkq2AYnCE
    challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.loginRapperChallenge, () => { return req.body.email === 'mc.safesearch@' + config.get<string>('application.domain') && req.body.password === 'Mr. N00dles' })
    challengeUtils.solveIf(challenges.loginAmyChallenge, () => { return req.body.email === 'amy@' + config.get<string>('application.domain') && req.body.password === 'K1f.....................' })
```

**Fix:** Move the credential out of source control into a secret store and rotate it → ❷ [M-032](#m-032) — Externalize the HMAC secret and remove plaintext credentials from source

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-798](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/798.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-033"></a><a id="f-033"></a>
#### F-033 · Password Hash with Insufficient Effort

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-08](#c-08) - Authentication & Session Surface  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:41`

**Issue:** `hash()` stores passwords as unsalted `MD5` (crypto.createHash('md5')). This is the hash written on password reset (`routes/resetPassword.ts:44` via `user.update`) and compared on 2FA setup/disable (`routes/2fa.ts:107`, 152).

`MD5` is a fast, unsalted digest: an attacker who reads the Users table (e.g. via auth-003 SQLi) recovers plaintext passwords using precomputed rainbow tables or GPU brute force at billions of guesses per second, and identical passwords produce identical hashes, exposing password reuse across accounts. Mass plaintext password recovery from any database read, enabling credential stuffing against other sites.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - Password hashing is unsalted `MD5` at `lib/insecurity.ts:41`, used as the credential-at-rest representation.

**Fix:** Replace the broken hash with a salted password-hashing function (bcrypt/Argon2id) → ❷ [M-033](#m-033) — Replace MD5 password hashing with bcrypt/argon2id and a per-user salt

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-916](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/916.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-034"></a><a id="f-034"></a>
#### F-034 · Incorrect Permission Assignment

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/ci.yml:1`

**Instances (6):** `.github/workflows/ci.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/release.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/rebase.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/zap_scan.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/stale.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/update-news-www.yml:1`

**Issue:** `ci.yml` has no top-level permissions: block. The workflow inherits the repository default GITHUB_TOKEN permissions (commonly write-all), so any compromised step can push code, create releases, or approve PRs.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - A sensitive resource is created with permissive default permissions.

```yaml
// .github/workflows/ci.yml:1
name: "CI/CD Pipeline"
on:
  push:
```

**Fix:** ❷ [M-034](#m-034) — Add `permissions: { contents: read }` at workflow root; elevate per-job only where needed

**Classification:** Error Information Disclosure · [CWE-732](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/732.html) · [OWASP A05:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A05_2021/)

<a id="t-035"></a><a id="f-035"></a>
#### F-035 · Third-party GitHub Action not pinned

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/ci.yml:188`

**Instances (3):** `.github/workflows/ci.yml:188`, `.github/workflows/codeql-analysis.yml:22`, `.github/workflows/image_actions.yml:30`

**Issue:** coverallsapp/github-action is referenced by the mutable @v2 tag. A compromised publisher could push malicious code to v2 and it would execute in all future workflow runs without any repo-side change.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous

```yaml
// .github/workflows/ci.yml:188
          name: api-test-lcov
      - name: "Publish coverage to Coveralls"
        uses: coverallsapp/github-action@v2
        with:
          github-token: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}
```

**Fix:** ❷ [M-035](#m-035) — Pin every third-party action to a full 40-char commit SHA

<a id="t-036"></a><a id="f-036"></a>
#### F-036 · Use of Unmaintained Third-Party Components

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - GitHub Actions CI/CD Pipeline  ·  **Location:** `Dockerfile:1`

**Instances (2):** `Dockerfile:1`, `test/smoke/Dockerfile:1`

**Issue:** The builder stage uses FROM node:24 without a @sha256: digest. A compromised or updated node:24 tag on Docker Hub could inject malicious code into every build without detection.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous

```dockerfile
// Dockerfile:1
```
