Strip directory components from entry names (use path.basename) so archive paths cannot influence the destination directory. Reject entries whose normalized name contains '..' segments or is absolute.

2. Strip directory components from entry names (use path.basename) so archive paths cannot influence the destination directory.
3. Reject entries whose normalized name contains '..' segments or is absolute.

```javascript
const base = path.resolve('uploads/complaints')
const dest = path.resolve(base, path.basename(entry.path))
if (!dest.startsWith(base + path.sep)) continue
await pipeline(entry.stream(), fs.createWriteStream(dest))
```

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `lib/insecurity.ts:42`

Remove the plaintext passwords at `routes/login.ts:60`-65 from source; if seed accounts are required, generate random passwords at seed time and store only hashes. Scrub both secrets from `git history and add a secret-scanning pre-commit hook (gitleaks)`.

2. Remove the plaintext passwords at `routes/login.ts:60`-65 from source; if seed accounts are required, generate random passwords at seed time and store only hashes.
3. Scrub both secrets from `git history and add a secret-scanning pre-commit hook (gitleaks)`.

```javascript
export const hmac = (data: string) =>
  crypto.createHmac('sha256', process.env.HMAC_KEY!).update(data).digest('hex')
```

<a id="m-033"></a>
#### M-033 — Replace MD5 password hashing with bcrypt/argon2id and a per-user salt

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-033](#f-033) — Weak Password Hash (`lib/insecurity.ts:41`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `lib/insecurity.ts:41`

**How:** Replace `crypto.createHash('md5')` at `lib/insecurity.ts:41` with a memory-hard KDF: bcrypt (cost >= 12) or argon2id. Migrate existing hashes lazily: on next successful login, re-hash the supplied password with the new algorithm and persist it. Ensure 2FA setup/disable (`routes/2fa.ts:107`, 152) and login (`routes/login.ts:34`) compare via the new verify function, not by hash equality on `MD5`.

1. Replace `crypto.createHash('md5')` at `lib/insecurity.ts:41` with a memory-hard KDF: bcrypt (cost >= 12) or argon2id.
2. Migrate existing hashes lazily: on next successful login, re-hash the supplied password with the new algorithm and persist it.
3. Ensure 2FA setup/disable (`routes/2fa.ts:107`, 152) and login (`routes/login.ts:34`) compare via the new verify function, not by hash equality on `MD5`.

```javascript
import bcrypt from 'bcryptjs'
export const hashPassword = (pw: string) => bcrypt.hashSync(pw, 12)
export const verifyPassword = (pw: string, stored: string) => bcrypt.compareSync(pw, stored)
```

#### M-037 — Encrypt the TOTP secret at rest with a KMS-managed key

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-037](#f-037) — TOTP 2FA secret stored as plaintext column on User model (`models/user.ts:112`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `models/user.ts:112`

**How:** Encrypt `totpSecret` with authenticated encryption (AES-256-GCM) using a key held outside the database, applied via a model setter/getter so the plaintext seed never persists. Ensure the secret is only decrypted transiently in memory during code verification and never serialized in API responses. Remove the cleartext `totpSecret` from `data/static/users.yml` seed data.
```javascript
totpSecret: {
  type: DataTypes.STRING,
  defaultValue: '',
  set (s: string) { this.setDataValue('totpSecret', s ? encryptAesGcm(s, process.env.TOTP_KEK) : '') },
  get () { const v = this.getDataValue('totpSecret'); return v ? decryptAesGcm(v, process.env.TOTP_KEK) : '' }
}
```

**Reference:** CWE-256

#### M-038 — Encrypt or tokenize cardholder PAN at rest and mask on retrieval in the Card model

- 🟠 [F-038](#f-038) — Cardholder PAN stored in plaintext without masking or encryption (`card.ts:38`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** High · **File:** `models/card.ts:38`

**How:** Stop storing the full PAN. Replace `cardNum` storage with a payment-processor token, or at minimum encrypt the PAN using authenticated encryption (AES-256-GCM) with a key held outside the database (KMS/env), applied in a model setter/getter pair.
```javascript
// models/card.ts — encrypt PAN at rest
cardNum: {
  type: DataTypes.STRING,
  set (pan: string) {
    this.setDataValue('cardNum', encryptAesGcm(String(pan), process.env.CARD_KEK))
  },
  get () { return maskLast4(decryptAesGcm(this.getDataValue('cardNum'))) }
}
```

<a id="m-041"></a>
#### M-041 — Replace MD5 password hashing with bcrypt/argon2id in the User model setter

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-041](#f-041) — MD5 unsalted password hashing in User model setter (`models/user.ts:76`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `models/user.ts:76`

**How:** Replace `security.hash()` in the `models/user.ts` password setter with a memory-hard adaptive KDF - bcrypt (cost >=12) or argon2id - using the already-present bcrypt dependency. Make the setter async-safe or hash in a `beforeSave` hook so the synchronous setter does not block; store the full KDF output (algorithm + cost + salt + digest) in the password column. Add a verification path that re-hashes legacy `MD5` values to the new KDF on next successful login, then drop the `MD5` code path. Re-seed `data/static/users.yml`-derived accounts through the new hashing path so no `MD5` digests remain.

1. Replace `security.hash()` in the `models/user.ts` password setter with a memory-hard adaptive KDF - bcrypt (cost >=12) or argon2id - using the already-present bcrypt dependency.
2. Make the setter async-safe or hash in a `beforeSave` hook so the synchronous setter does not block; store the full KDF output (algorithm + cost + salt + digest) in the password column.
3. Add a verification path that re-hashes legacy `MD5` values to the new KDF on next successful login, then drop the `MD5` code path.
4. Re-seed `data/static/users.yml`-derived accounts through the new hashing path so no `MD5` digests remain.

```javascript
import bcrypt from 'bcryptjs'
// in models/user.ts password field:
set (clearTextPassword: string) {
  // store full bcrypt hash (salt+cost embedded)
  this.setDataValue('password', bcrypt.hashSync(clearTextPassword, 12))
}
```

**Reference:** https://`cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Password_Storage_Cheat_Sheet.html`

<a id="m-044"></a>
#### M-044 — Remove poison-null-byte truncation and enforce extension allowlist on the post-decode filename

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-044](#f-044) — Poison-null-byte path read bypass in FTP file server (`routes/fileServer.ts:33`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `routes/fileServer.ts:33`

**How:** Delete the `cutOffPoisonNullByte` call so the filename is never silently truncated after validation; reject any name containing a NUL or %00 sequence outright with a 400. Re-derive and re-check the extension on the exact byte string passed to res.`sendFile`, after URL-decoding, so the allowlist and the served path can never diverge. Constrain the resolved path to the ftp/ root: compute `path.resolve('ftp', file)` and verify it `startsWith` `path.resolve('ftp')` + `path.sep` before `sendFile`.

1. Delete the `cutOffPoisonNullByte` call so the filename is never silently truncated after validation; reject any name containing a NUL or %00 sequence outright with a 400.
2. Re-derive and re-check the extension on the exact byte string passed to res.`sendFile`, after URL-decoding, so the allowlist and the served path can never diverge.
3. Constrain the resolved path to the ftp/ root: compute `path.resolve('ftp', file)` and verify it `startsWith` `path.resolve('ftp')` + `path.sep` before `sendFile`.

```javascript
const decoded = decodeURIComponent(file)
if (decoded.includes('\u0000')) return res.sendStatus(400)
if (!/\.(md|pdf)$/i.test(decoded)) return res.sendStatus(403)
const abs = path.resolve('ftp', decoded)
if (!abs.startsWith(path.resolve('ftp') + path.sep)) return res.sendStatus(403)
res.sendFile(abs)
```

**Reference:** CWE-22

<a id="m-047"></a>
#### M-047 — Scope challenge-solved events to the solving principal and strip flags from broadcast payloads

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-047](#f-047) — Challenge-solved broadcast leaks CTF flags to every connected client

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `lib/challengeUtils.ts:75`

**How:** Replace the global `io.emit('challenge solved', ...)` with a room/namespace emit targeting only the `socket(s)` belonging to the user who solved the challenge (`io.to(userRoom).emit(...)`). Remove the `flag` field from any payload sent to clients other than the solver; deliver flags only to the authenticated owner. Stop replaying the full global `notifications` backlog to every new connection; replay only the connecting principal's own notifications after authentication.

1. Replace the global `io.emit('challenge solved', ...)` with a room/namespace emit targeting only the `socket(s)` belonging to the user who solved the challenge (`io.to(userRoom).emit(...)`).
2. Remove the `flag` field from any payload sent to clients other than the solver; deliver flags only to the authenticated owner.
3. Stop replaying the full global `notifications` backlog to every new connection; replay only the connecting principal's own notifications after authentication.

```javascript
// emit only to the solver's room, without the flag for others
const { flag, ...publicNotification } = notification
io.to(`user:${solverId}`).emit('challenge solved', notification)
io.except(`user:${solverId}`).emit('challenge solved', publicNotification)
```

<a id="m-048"></a>
#### M-048 — Replace substring redirect check with exact-origin URL parsing in isRedirectAllowed

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-048](#f-048) — Open redirect via substring allowlist match (`insecurity.ts:136`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `lib/insecurity.ts:133`

**How:** In `lib/insecurity.ts:133`, parse `toUrl` with `new URL(toUrl)` and compare the parsed `.origin` (or full normalized href) against entries in `redirectAllowlist` using strict equality - never `String.includes`. Reject any URL that fails to parse, uses a non-https scheme, or whose origin is not an exact member of the allowlist; return 406 as `routes/redirect.ts:21` already does for the disallowed branch. Add a unit test asserting that `https://attacker.test/?x=https://github.com/juice-shop/juice-shop` is rejected.

1. In `lib/insecurity.ts:133`, parse `toUrl` with `new URL(toUrl)` and compare the parsed `.origin` (or full normalized href) against entries in `redirectAllowlist` using strict equality - never `String.includes`.
2. Reject any URL that fails to parse, uses a non-https scheme, or whose origin is not an exact member of the allowlist; return 406 as `routes/redirect.ts:21` already does for the disallowed branch.
3. Add a unit test asserting that `https://attacker.test/?x=https://github.com/juice-shop/juice-shop` is rejected.

```javascript
export const isRedirectAllowed = (url: string) => {
  let target: URL
  try { target = new URL(url) } catch { return false }
  if (target.protocol !== 'https:') return false
  return [...redirectAllowlist].some(a => {
    try { return new URL(a).origin === target.origin } catch { return false }
  })
}
```

**Reference:** https://`cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Unvalidated_Redirects_and_Forwards_Cheat_Sheet.html`

<a id="m-059"></a>
#### M-059 — Reject active image formats and re-encode uploaded profile images server-side

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-059](#f-059) — Polyglot/MIME-spoofed image upload via magic-byte-only check

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/profileImageFileUpload.ts:24`

**How:** Restrict accepted types to a strict raster allowlist (png, jpeg) and explicitly reject svg and any format that can carry script. Re-encode every accepted upload through an image library (e.g. sharp) to strip embedded payloads before persisting. Serve uploaded images from a distinct sandbox origin (or with Content-Disposition: attachment and a restrictive Content-Security-Policy) so a polyglot cannot execute in the app origin.

1. Restrict accepted types to a strict raster allowlist (png, jpeg) and explicitly reject svg and any format that can carry script.
2. Re-encode every accepted upload through an image library (e.g. sharp) to strip embedded payloads before persisting.
3. Serve uploaded images from a distinct sandbox origin (or with Content-Disposition: attachment and a restrictive Content-Security-Policy) so a polyglot cannot execute in the app origin.

```javascript
import sharp from 'sharp'
if (!['image/png','image/jpeg'].includes(uploadedFileType.mime)) { res.status(415); return next(new Error('type not allowed')) }
const safe = await sharp(buffer).png().toBuffer()
await fs.writeFile(filePath, safe)
```

**Reference:** https://`cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/File_Upload_Cheat_Sheet.html`

---

<a id="m-060"></a>
#### M-060 — Validate the Origin handshake header and bind sessions to handshake tokens (not ambient cookies)

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-060](#f-060) — WebSocket upgrade has no Origin enforcement enabling cross-site hijacking

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20`

**How:** Drive the allowed origin list from configuration per environment instead of the hardcoded `http://localhost:4200`, and validate `socket.handshake.headers.origin` against that allowlist inside `io.use()`, rejecting mismatches. Authenticate the channel with an explicit handshake token (`socket.handshake.auth.token`) rather than relying on ambient cookies, so a cross-origin page cannot ride the victim's session. Set the Socket\.IO server `transports`/`allowRequest` callback to reject upgrades whose Origin is absent or not in the allowlist.

1. Drive the allowed origin list from configuration per environment instead of the hardcoded `http://localhost:4200`, and validate `socket.handshake.headers.origin` against that allowlist inside `io.use()`, rejecting mismatches.
2. Authenticate the channel with an explicit handshake token (`socket.handshake.auth.token`) rather than relying on ambient cookies, so a cross-origin page cannot ride the victim's session.
3. Set the Socket\.IO server `transports`/`allowRequest` callback to reject upgrades whose Origin is absent or not in the allowlist.

```javascript
const allowed = config.get('app.allowedOrigins') // per-env
const io = new Server(server, {
  cors: { origin: allowed },
  allowRequest: (req, cb) => cb(allowed.includes(req.headers.origin) ? null : 'forbidden', allowed.includes(req.headers.origin))
})
```

**Reference:** CWE-346

---

<a id="m-061"></a>
#### M-061 — Add anti-CSRF tokens and SameSite cookies to state-changing auth endpoints

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-061](#f-061) — Missing CSRF Protection (`server.ts:596`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `lib/insecurity.ts:192`

**How:** Set SameSite=Strict (and HttpOnly, Secure) on the token cookie issued in `updateAuthenticatedUsers()` (`lib/insecurity.ts:192`). Require a synchronizer or double-submit CSRF token on 2FA setup/disable (`routes/2fa.ts:97`, 142) and password reset (`routes/resetPassword.ts`). Prefer the Authorization: Bearer header for the SPA and reject cookie-based token admission for state-changing routes so cross-site cookie auth cannot occur.

1. Set SameSite=Strict (and HttpOnly, Secure) on the token cookie issued in `updateAuthenticatedUsers()` (`lib/insecurity.ts:192`).
2. Require a synchronizer or double-submit CSRF token on 2FA setup/disable (`routes/2fa.ts:97`, 142) and password reset (`routes/resetPassword.ts`).
3. Prefer the Authorization: Bearer header for the SPA and reject cookie-based token admission for state-changing routes so cross-site cookie auth cannot occur.

```javascript
import csrf from 'csurf'
const csrfProtection = csrf({ cookie: { httpOnly: true, sameSite: 'strict' } })
app.post('/rest/2fa/disable', csrfProtection, twoFactorDisable)
```

**Reference:** https://`cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Cross-Site_Request_Forgery_Prevention_Cheat_Sheet.html`

<a id="m-062"></a>
#### M-062 — Enforce coupon eligibility server-side and remove secrets from the system prompt

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-062](#f-062) — Chatbot prompt injection and tool abuse via unbounded user messages

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/chat.ts:191`

**How:** Validate coupon eligibility and the 10% cap in the `generateCoupon` `execute()` handler in code, not via prompt instructions - reject discount > 10 regardless of model output. Remove the CONFIDENTIAL discount instruction from the system prompt; keep business rules server-side. Add input/output guardrails (content filtering) and never expose privileged tools to unauthenticated chat sessions.

1. Validate coupon eligibility and the 10% cap in the `generateCoupon` `execute()` handler in code, not via prompt instructions - reject discount > 10 regardless of model output.
2. Remove the CONFIDENTIAL discount instruction from the system prompt; keep business rules server-side.
3. Add input/output guardrails (content filtering) and never expose privileged tools to unauthenticated chat sessions.

```javascript
execute: async ({ discount }) => {
  const capped = Math.min(discount, 10)
  if (!await orderEligibleForCoupon(req)) return { error: 'not eligible' }
  return { couponCode: security.generateCoupon(capped), discount: capped }
}
```

**Reference:** https://genai.owasp.org/llmrisk/llm01-prompt-injection/

<a id="m-063"></a>
#### M-063 — Emit structured append-only audit events for all authentication state changes

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-063](#f-063) — Missing Security Event Logging

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/login.ts:32`

**How:** Log a structured event (actor id/email, source IP, user-agent, outcome, UTC timestamp, event type) on each login success and failure in `routes/login.ts`. Add the same logging to 2FA verify/setup/disable (`routes/2fa.ts`) and password reset (`routes/resetPassword.ts`). Write events to an append-only sink (e.g. a write-once log table or external SIEM) so they cannot be edited by an application-level compromise. Do not log the password, the JWT, or the TOTP secret.

1. Log a structured event (actor id/email, source IP, user-agent, outcome, UTC timestamp, event type) on each login success and failure in `routes/login.ts`.
2. Add the same logging to 2FA verify/setup/disable (`routes/2fa.ts`) and password reset (`routes/resetPassword.ts`).
3. Write events to an append-only sink (e.g. a write-once log table or external SIEM) so they cannot be edited by an application-level compromise.
4. Do not log the password, the JWT, or the TOTP secret.

```javascript
logger.info({
  event: 'login_success', userId: user.id, ip: req.ip,
  ua: req.headers['user-agent'], ts: new Date().toISOString()
})
```

**Reference:** CWE-778

<a id="m-066"></a>
#### M-066 — Validate and allowlist the LLM endpoint and authenticate the upstream

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-066](#f-066) — LLM base URL sourced from writable config enables SSRF on startup (`chat.ts:111`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/chat.ts:111`

**How:** Validate application.`chatBot`.`llmApiUrl` at startup against an allowlist of permitted hosts/schemes; refuse to start if it resolves to an unexpected or non-loopback address in production. Require LLM_API_KEY (or `mTLS`) for the upstream provider instead of defaulting to an empty key, so a redirected endpoint cannot silently impersonate the model. Restrict who can read/write the live application configuration so the URL cannot be altered at runtime by lower-privileged actors.

1. Validate application.`chatBot`.`llmApiUrl` at startup against an allowlist of permitted hosts/schemes; refuse to start if it resolves to an unexpected or non-loopback address in production.
2. Require LLM_API_KEY (or `mTLS`) for the upstream provider instead of defaulting to an empty key, so a redirected endpoint cannot silently impersonate the model.
3. Restrict who can read/write the live application configuration so the URL cannot be altered at runtime by lower-privileged actors.

```javascript
const url = new URL(config.get('application.chatBot.llmApiUrl'))
if (!ALLOWED_LLM_HOSTS.has(url.host)) throw new Error('LLM endpoint not allowlisted')
```

<a id="m-069"></a>
#### M-069 — Isolate ORG_ADMIN_TOKEN out of the pull_request_target workflow

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-069](#f-069) — Privileged PR Trigger Exposes Org-Admin Token (`pr-compliance.yml:4`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `.github/workflows/pr-compliance.yml:4`

**How:** Split the privileged 'Block Spammer' action into a separate workflow triggered by workflow_run (after the untrusted-data job completes) so ORG_ADMIN_TOKEN is never present in the same job that processes untrusted PR metadata. Scope ORG_ADMIN_TOKEN to the minimum (a fine-grained token limited to org-block, not full admin) and rotate it. Add a CI guard (e.g. zizmor) that fails the build if pull_request_target is ever combined with a checkout of github.event.pull_request.head.* or with \${{ github.event.pull_request.* }} interpolated into a run/script body.

1. Split the privileged 'Block Spammer' action into a separate workflow triggered by workflow_run (after the untrusted-data job completes) so ORG_ADMIN_TOKEN is never present in the same job that processes untrusted PR metadata.
2. Scope ORG_ADMIN_TOKEN to the minimum (a fine-grained token limited to org-block, not full admin) and rotate it.
3. Add a CI guard (e.g. zizmor) that fails the build if pull_request_target is ever combined with a checkout of github.event.pull_request.head.* or with \${{ github.event.pull_request.* }} interpolated into a run/script body.

```javascript
# pull_request_target job: read-only, untrusted-data handling only
# separate workflow_run job: holds ORG_ADMIN_TOKEN, no untrusted input
```

**Reference:** https://securitylab.github.com/resources/github-actions-preventing-pwn-requests/

<a id="m-071"></a>
#### M-071 — Use a production-safe error handler that hides internals

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-071](#f-071) — Verbose errorhandler leaks stack traces in responses (`server.ts:682`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `server.ts:189`

**How:** Only mount `errorhandler()` when NODE_ENV !== 'production'; otherwise use a handler that returns a generic message and a correlation id. Log the full error server-side, return only `{ error: 'Internal Server Error', id }` to the client. Ensure x-powered-by and version banners are suppressed (x-powered-by is already disabled at `server.ts:189`).

1. Only mount `errorhandler()` when NODE_ENV !== 'production'; otherwise use a handler that returns a generic message and a correlation id.
2. Log the full error server-side, return only `{ error: 'Internal Server Error', id }` to the client.
3. Ensure x-powered-by and version banners are suppressed (x-powered-by is already disabled at `server.ts:189`).

```javascript
if (process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production') app.use(errorhandler())
else app.use((err, req, res, _next) => { logger.error(err); res.status(500).json({ error: 'Internal Server Error' }) })
```

**Reference:** https://`cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Error_Handling_Cheat_Sheet.html`

<a id="m-072"></a>
#### M-072 — Load HMAC/token secrets from configuration and rotate the exposed keys

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-072](#f-072) — Hardcoded HMAC secret used for coupon and deluxe tokens (`lib/insecurity.ts:42`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `lib/insecurity.ts:42`

**How:** Source the HMAC key from `process.env` / secrets manager, not an inline literal, and rotate the exposed value. Use a dedicated entitlement secret for `deluxeToken` rather than reusing the JWT private key. Bind deluxe entitlement to a server-side record rather than a client-presented HMAC token.

1. Source the HMAC key from `process.env` / secrets manager, not an inline literal, and rotate the exposed value.
2. Use a dedicated entitlement secret for `deluxeToken` rather than reusing the JWT private key.
3. Bind deluxe entitlement to a server-side record rather than a client-presented HMAC token.

```javascript
const HMAC_KEY = process.env.HMAC_KEY
export const hmac = (data: string) => crypto.createHmac('sha256', HMAC_KEY).update(data).digest('hex')
```

**Reference:** https://`cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Secrets_Management_Cheat_Sheet.html`

```javascript
if: >-
  github.event.issue.pull_request != '' &&
  contains(github.event.comment.body, '/rebase') &&
  contains(fromJSON('["OWNER","MEMBER","COLLABORATOR"]'), github.event.comment.author_association)
```

<a id="m-076"></a>
#### M-076 — Add rate limiting and bounded deserialization to the /file-upload endpoint

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-076](#f-076) — YAML deserialization bomb and XXE timeout DoS on `/file-upload`

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/fileUpload.ts:109`

**How:** Apply express-rate-limit to `POST /file-upload` to cap requests per IP and blunt volumetric deserialization-bomb attacks. Use a YAML loader configured with anchor/alias limits (or js-yaml FAILSAFE_SCHEMA) and a hard `node count cap so anchor expansion cannot blow up before the timeout`. Run untrusted XML/YAML parsing in a resource-limited worker thread rather than vm.`runInContext`, which does not bound memory.

1. Apply express-rate-limit to `POST /file-upload` to cap requests per IP and blunt volumetric deserialization-bomb attacks.
2. Use a YAML loader configured with anchor/alias limits (or js-yaml FAILSAFE_SCHEMA) and a hard `node count cap so anchor expansion cannot blow up before the timeout`.
3. Run untrusted XML/YAML parsing in a resource-limited worker thread rather than vm.`runInContext`, which does not bound memory.

```javascript
import rateLimit from 'express-rate-limit'
app.post('/file-upload', rateLimit({ windowMs: 60000, max: 20 }), uploadToMemory.single('file'), /* ... */)
```

**Reference:** https://`cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Denial_of_Service_Cheat_Sheet.html`

<a id="m-077"></a>
#### M-077 — Apply per-IP connection caps, message throttling, and a bounded maxHttpBufferSize to the Socket\.IO server

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-077](#f-077) — Socket\.IO server has no connection or message rate limiting

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20`

**How:** Set a conservative `maxHttpBufferSize` on the `new Server(...)` options to bound per-message payload size. Add per-IP connection accounting in `io.use()` (or via a Redis adapter / reverse-proxy limit) and reject new connections above a threshold. Throttle inbound `verify*` and `notification received` events per socket (e.g. a token-bucket on `socket.data`) so a single client cannot flood regex-bearing handlers on the event loop.

1. Set a conservative `maxHttpBufferSize` on the `new Server(...)` options to bound per-message payload size.
2. Add per-IP connection accounting in `io.use()` (or via a Redis adapter / reverse-proxy limit) and reject new connections above a threshold.
3. Throttle inbound `verify*` and `notification received` events per socket (e.g. a token-bucket on `socket.data`) so a single client cannot flood regex-bearing handlers on the event loop.

```javascript
const io = new Server(server, {
  cors: { origin: allowed },
  maxHttpBufferSize: 1e4,        // bound message size
  pingTimeout: 20000
})
io.use(perIpConnectionLimiter(20)) // reject > 20 conns / IP
```

**Reference:** CWE-770

---

### P4 — Backlog

_No P4 mitigations._

---

## 11. Out of Scope

The following items are **explicitly excluded** from this threat model. Findings against these areas should be tracked separately.

- Third-party hosted dependencies and SaaS endpoints
- Browser runtime vulnerabilities and end-user device security
- Operating system kernel and container runtime
- Underlying network infrastructure (DNS, BGP, ISP)
- Physical security of hosting facilities

| Phase 11 | Finalization Substeps 1-3 - yaml built (77<br/>threats), baseline cached | threat-analyst (sonnet-4-6) | 2m30s |
| Phase 11 | Management summary (RENDER_ROLE=ms) | threat-analyst (sonnet-4-6) | 3m 52s |
| Phase 11 | [§7](#7-security-architecture) enrichment (secarch) - done | threat-analyst (sonnet-4-6) | 5m 29s |

<a id="appendix-composition-notes"></a>
## Appendix: Composition Notes

The composition pipeline emitted the soft warnings listed below. These do not block release (the contract still passed) but they flag content the renderer could not fully validate - typically NARRATIVE_PLACEHOLDER leakage from Stage-2 incomplete authoring or Mermaid syntax that downstream parsers may reject.

### Soft Warnings

| Section | Category | Detail |
|----------------------|-----------|----------------------|
| Global Secret-Mask Pass | `secret_mask` | secret-mask applied:<br/>generic_credential_assignment -<br/>credential-shaped strings were redacted to <REDACTED><br/>placeholders |
| (unspecified) | `other` | stripped 2 leaked '' comments before final<br/>write (these should flow via<br/>.qa-repair-plan.json) |

<a id="appendix-a-vektor-taxonomy"></a>
## Appendix A — Vektor Taxonomy

This appendix defines the attacker-starting-position labels used in the Top Threats table and throughout [§8 Findings Register](#8-findings-register). Each label answers the question *what does the attacker need before the exploit begins?*

<a id="vektor-internet-anon"></a>
### Internet Anon

**Attacker position:** Unauthenticated attacker from the public internet · **Breach distance:** 1

**Preconditions:**

- Endpoint is reachable from the internet (no IP allowlist, no VPN)
- No authentication middleware blocks the request

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html) · [CWE-79](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/79.html) · [CWE-306](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/306.html) · [CWE-327](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/327.html) · [CWE-611](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/611.html) · [CWE-918](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/918.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A01:2021, A03:2021, A07:2021

<a id="vektor-internet-user"></a>
### Internet User

**Attacker position:** Any authenticated low-privilege user (valid JWT / session) · **Breach distance:** 2

**Preconditions:**

- Attacker has signed up or otherwise obtained a valid user session
- Endpoint is behind auth but not behind role/admin checks

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-434](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/434.html) · [CWE-611](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/611.html) · [CWE-918](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/918.html) · [CWE-352](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/352.html) · [CWE-287](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/287.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A01:2021, A04:2021, A05:2021, A10:2021

<a id="vektor-internet-priv-user"></a>
### Internet Priv User

**Attacker position:** Authenticated admin-level user (JWT with admin role or equivalent) · **Breach distance:** 2

**Preconditions:**

- Attacker holds admin credentials or has elevated privileges
- Endpoint gated on admin role but still exploitable once reached

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-862](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/862.html) · [CWE-79](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/79.html) · [CWE-94](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/94.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A01:2021

<a id="vektor-victim-required"></a>
### Victim-Required

**Attacker position:** Attacker needs victim interaction - social engineering, crafted link, or live session · **Breach distance:** 2

**Preconditions:**

- Victim must click a link, load a page, or have an active session
- Applies to XSS, CSRF, click-jacking, open redirect

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-79](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/79.html) · [CWE-352](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/352.html) · [CWE-601](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/601.html) · [CWE-1021](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1021.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A01:2021, A03:2021

<a id="vektor-build-time"></a>
### Build-Time

**Attacker position:** Attacker controls a build input - CI runner, dependency, base image, or external data fetched during build · **Breach distance:** 3

**Preconditions:**

- Compromise of a dependency, registry, or base image
- OR compromise of a CI runner with write access to artifacts

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-506](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/506.html) · [CWE-829](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/829.html) · [CWE-1039](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1039.html) · [CWE-1104](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1104.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A08:2021

<a id="vektor-repo-read"></a>
### Repo-Read

**Attacker position:** Attacker gains read access to source repository (leaked clone, forked fork, insider, compromised developer workstation) · **Breach distance:** 3

**Preconditions:**

- Read access to the source tree at or after commit time
- No runtime exploit needed - the vulnerability is the content of the repo

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-798](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/798.html) · [CWE-312](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/312.html) · [CWE-540](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/540.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A02:2021, A07:2021

<a id="vektor-n-a"></a>
### n/a

**Attacker position:** Architectural / meta-finding - no runtime entry point, the finding describes a design defect aggregating multiple code-level findings

**Preconditions:**

- Finding is AF-NNN (architectural) rather than F-NNN (code-level)
